In the earlier part of our order, we have expressed our views about the acceptability of the statement of Md. Usman Jan Khan (PW2), validity of the confessional statement of the accused as well as coaccused implicating the appellant (A15) and his relationship with Tiger as well as the part played by him in association with him.	None
Learned counsel for the appellant prayed for discarding his confession.	None
However, in view of the explanation and the evidence of I.O.s and recording officers, discussion and ultimate conclusion of the Designated Court, we reject her request.	None
The appellants involvement in landing, his association with Tiger Memon, participation in planting scooter bomb have been fully established by the prosecution.	None
We agree with the conclusion arrived at by the Designated Court.	None
Sentence Even at the beginning, Ms. Farhana Shah, learned counsel appearing for the appellant highlighted that out of the life imprisonment, the appellant had served nearly 14 years in jail.	Arguments of Petitioner
She also highlighted that the appellant is suffering with AIDS HIV and is a sick person.	Arguments of Petitioner
She also placed his treatment particulars furnished by J.J. Hospital and recent medical reports showing his CD Count and his Blood Count.	Arguments of Petitioner
She further pointed out that in spite of continuous treatment, even at this stage, he is suffering from AIDS.	Arguments of Petitioner
As a matter of fact, considering his health condition, this Court has granted him interim bail on medical grounds and that is being continued even now.	None
The fact that the appellant is suffering from AIDS HIV has not been disputed by the CBI.	None
Taking note of all these aspects including the fact that he was in jail nearly for 14 years, while confirming the conviction and sentence, in view of special circumstances, though the life sentence is the appropriate sentence for the proved charges, we order that there is no need to send him back to prison.	None
In the peculiar circumstance, we make it clear that the period already undergone would be sufficient and with this direction, we dispose of his appeal.	Decision
Criminal Appeal No. 1224 of 2007 Smt.	Decision
Vimal Thapa W o Late Somnath Kakaram Thapa (A112) Appellant(s) vs. The State of Maharashtra Respondent(s)	None
Mr. Jaspal Singh, learned counsel appeared for the appellant, who is wife of A112 and Mr. Mukul Gupta learned senior counsel duly assisted by Mr. Satyakam, learned counsel for the respondent (CBI).	None
Late Shri S.K. Thapa Accused No. 112 died during the pendency of this appeal because of lungs cancer.	Issue
His widow has stepped in and is pursuing this appeal.	Issue
The above said appeal is directed against the final judgment and order of conviction and sentence dated 28.11.2006 and 20.07.2007 respectively, whereby A112 (husband of the appellant herein) was convicted and sentenced to rigorous imprisonment (RI) for life by the Designated Court under TADA for the Bombay Bomb Blast Case, Greater Bombay in B.B.C. No.1/1993.	Issue
Late Shri S.K. Thapa belonged to the 1972 batch of Indian Custom Excise Service.	None
In the year 1993, he was posted as Additional Collector of Marine and Preventive Wing of Customs, Collectorate at Bombay.	None
The other wing of the Collectorate was Rummaging and Intelligence and at the relevant time, Shri M.N. Dholphode (PW171) was the Additional Collector and the Customs (Preventive) Collectorate was headed by Shri S.K. Bhardwaj (PW 470).	None
Charges A common charge of conspiracy was framed against all the co conspirators including A112.	Facts
The relevant portion of the said charge is reproduced hereunder During the period from December, 1992 to April, 1993 at various places in Bombay, District Raigad and District Thane in India and outside India in Dubai (U.A.E.) and Pakistan, entered into a criminal conspiracy and or were members of the said criminal conspiracy whose object was to commit terrorist acts in India and that you all agreed to commit following illegal acts, namely, to commit terrorist acts with an intent to overawe the Government as by law established, to strike terror in the people, to alienate sections of the people and to adversely affect the harmony amongst different sections of the people, i.e. Hindus and Muslims by using bombs, dynamites, hand grenades and other explosive substances like RDX or inflammable substances or fire arms like AK56 rifles, carbines, pistols and other lethal weapons, in such a manner as to cause or as likely to cause death of or injuries to any person or persons, loss of or damage to and disruption of supplies of services essential to the life of the community, and to achieve the objectives of the conspiracy, you all agreed to smuggle firearms, ammunitions, detonators, hand grenades and high explosives like RDX into India and to distribute the same amongst yourselves and your men of confidence for the purpose of committing terrorist acts and for the said purpose to conceal and store all these arms, ammunitions and explosives at such safe places and amongst yourselves and with your men of confidence till its use for committing terrorist acts and achieving the objects of criminal conspiracy and to dispose off the same as need arises.	Facts
To organize training camps in Pakistan and in India to import and undergo weapons training in handling of arms, ammunitions and explosives to commit terrorist acts.	Facts
To harbour and conceal terrorists coconspirators, and also to aid, abet and knowingly facilitate the terrorist acts and or any act preparatory to the commission of terrorist acts and to render any assistance financial or otherwise for accomplishing the object of the conspiracy to commit terrorist acts, to do and commit any other illegal acts as were necessary for achieving the aforesaid objectives of the criminal conspiracy and that on 12.03.1993 were successful in causing bomb explosions at Stock Exchange Building, Air India Building, Hotel Sea Rock at Bandra, Hotel Centaur at Juhu, Hotel Centaur at Santacruz, Zaveri Bazaar, Katha Bazaar, Century Bazaar at Worli, Petrol Pump adjoining Shiv Sena Bhavan, Plaza Theatre and in lobbing handgrenades at Macchimar Hindu Colony, Mahim and at Bay52, Sahar International Airport which left more than 257 persons dead, 713 injured and property worth about Rs.27 crores destroyed, and attempted to cause bomb explosions at Naigaum Cross Road and Dhanji Street, all in the city of Bombay and its suburbs i.e. within Greater Bombay.	Facts
And thereby committed offences punishable under Section 3(3) of TADA (P) Act, 1987 and Section 120B of IPC read with Sections 3(2)(i)(ii), 3(3)(4), 5 and 6 of TADA (P) Act, 1987 and read with Sections 302, 307, 326, 324, 427, 435, 436, 201 and 212 of Indian Penal Code and offences under Sections 3 and 7 read with Sections 25 (1A), (1B)(a) of the Arms Act, 1959, Sections 9B (1)(a)(b)(c) of the Explosives Act, 1884, Sections 3, 4(a)(b), 5 and 6 of the Explosive Substances Act, 1908 and Section 4 of the Prevention of Damage to Public Property Act, 1984 and within my cognizance.	Facts
In addition to the abovesaid principal charge of conspiracy, A112 was also charged on the following counts In addition, to Charge First, you accused, Somnath Kakaram Thapa is also charged for having committed the following offences in pursuance to the Criminal Conspiracy described in Charge First  At head Secondly That you Somnath Kakaram Thapa during the period you were posted as Additional Collector of Customs, Preventive, Bombay and particularly during the period from January, 1993 to February, 1993 in pursuance of the aforesaid criminal conspiracy and in furtherance of its object abetted and knowingly facilitated the commission of terrorists acts and acts preparatory to terrorists act, i.e., bomb blast and such other acts which were committed in Bombay and its suburbs on 12.03.1993 by intentionally aiding, and abetting Dawood Ibrahim Kaskar, Mohmed Dosa and Mushtaq Ibrahim Tiger Abdul Razak Memon and their associates and knowingly facilitated smuggling of arms, ammunitions and explosives which were smuggled into India by Dawood Ibrahim Kaskar, Mohammed Dossa, Mushtaq Ibrahim Tiger Abdul Razak Memon and their associates for the purpose of committing terrorists acts by your non interference inspite of the fact that you had specific information and knowledge that arms, ammunitions and explosives were being smuggled into the country by terrorists and as Additional Collector of Customs, Preventive, you were legally bound to prevent it and that you thereby committed an offence punishable under Section 3(3) of TADA (P) Act,1987 and within my cognizance.	Facts
The charges mentioned above were proved against A112 and he had been convicted and sentenced for the above said charges as under Conviction and Sentence A112 has been convicted for the offence of conspiracy under Section 3(3) of TADA and Section 120B of IPC read with the offences described at head firstly and sentenced to RI for life along with a fine of Rs. 1,00,000/, in default, to further undergo RI for 3 years.	None
(charge firstly) ii) A112 has also been convicted under Section 3(3) of TADA for commission of offences at head secondly and sentenced to RI for life along with a fine of Rs. 1,00,000/, in default, to further undergo RI for 3 years.	Facts
(charge secondly)	None

Deposition of Prosecution Witnesses Apart from the aforesaid evidence, the involvement and the role of A112 in the conspiracy, as stated above, is disclosed by the deposition of various prosecution witnesses which are as under Deposition of Akbarkhan Munawarkhan Pathan (PW98) PW98 was an Inspector posted in the Night Mobile Patrolling Unit of Marine and Prevention Wing of Customs Department.	None
From his deposition, the following facts emerge He knew A112 as he was his superior officer in the year 1993.	None
PW98 identified A112 in the court during the dock proceedings.	None
On 30.01.1993, A112 gave instructions to other officers to assemble in the Thane office.	None
After the meeting, they all first went to Indraprastha Hotel at Nagothane and then reached Purar Phata in Raigad district by sunset following A112.	None
PW98 deposed that A112 gave officers their positions at the spot.	None
PW98 deposed that A112 told the officers that contraband was to be smuggled into India by Tiger Memon and he will be coming in a commander jeep and would be sitting next to the driver with his body guards sitting at the rear side, fully armed and in a ready position to fire.	None
A112 also told the officers that a truck or tempo will be carrying the contraband following the jeep.	None
PW98 deposed that A112 told that they have to intercept the convoy and affect the seizure.	None
PW98 deposed that they took positions and waited at the spot for about 5 hours upto midnight and thereafter A112 called them up and asked to be in touch with him in Bombay office.	None
Thereafter, the operation was called off.	None
On 31.01.1993, the officers along with A112 went to Dehan Phata where he gave the same instructions as given at Purar Phata and surveillance was kept for the same person (Tiger Memon).	None
After waiting for six hours, A112 called off the ambush as no convoy arrived carrying contraband.	None
Thereafter, no instructions were received from A112 after 31.01.1993.	None

Nos. 530 and 531, Reports prepared by him about the operations at Purar Phata and Dehan Phata in the night of 30/31.01.1993 respectively.	None

PW98 deposed that he does not remember the junction today but stated that A112 told Mr. Agarkar that the said place was the best place to keep the watch and as per the information, the said place was the perfect place for interception.	None

PW98 and Mr. Mhatre were also there in that party.	None
Upon perusal of the aforesaid deposition, it is clear that A112 had specific information that contraband was being smuggled into India by Tiger Memon and will be transported in a Truck or Tempo and that Tiger Memon will accompany the same and will be seated next to the driver and body guards will sit in the rear side armed with guns in ready to shoot position. Deposition of Madhav Sriram Agharkar (PW99) PW99 was an Inspector of Customs (Marine and Preventive) Wing.	None
From his testimony, the following facts emerge A112 called him on 30.01.1993 and told him to reach Thane office.	None

As the information had revealed that the contraband silver was to be landed somewhere at Shekhadi and Shrivardhan area and the same was to be transported via MhasalaGoregaon road, PW99 suggested him two spots for keeping a watch at Purar Phata and Dehan Phata A112 asked all of them to leave the Thane Office and to proceed towards Nagothane.	None
He also accompanied them.	None
All the officers including A112 left Nagothane at about 5.00 p.m. and went to Purar Phata and reached there by sunset.	None
After reaching Purar Phata, A112 called the other Inspectors who were accompanying the squad and disclosed the information that the contraband silver would be transported in transport vehicles such as Truck or Tempo and that Tiger Memon would be piloting the said transport vehicles in the open Commander Jeep and he would be sitting beside the driver with three to four bodyguards sitting behind him and all of them would be fully armed.	None
Before taking positions at Purar Phata, PW99 told A112 that junction of Mhsala Saimorbaugh Mangaon Road and Mhsala Goregaon Road would be better for keeping surveillance and suggested the said spot in order to cover both the said routes coming from Mhasala to Bombay.	None
A112 responded and said that his information was specific that goods will go through Purar Phata Road.	None
At about midnight, A112 called off the watch operation Again, they went to Dehan Phata where A112 told them that the previous day information was also for Dehan Phata.	None
Thereafter, the operation was called off at midnight by A112 who also told that he will give information if watch has to be continued on the next day.	None
PW99 deposed that no information was received from A112.	None

Nos. 530 and 531 which were prepared by PW98.	None
He identified A112 before the court.	None
In the second week of February 1993, A112 had asked PW99 to find out whether any chemical in liquid form, packed in barrels, had been landed by Tiger Memon at Shekhadi.	None
Hence, the deposition of PW99 corroborates and supports the deposition of PW98.	None
Mr. Jaspal Singh, learned counsel for the defence contended that A 112 acted immediately after he received the information about landing smuggling of arms and set up an ambush.	Arguments of Petitioner
The fact that ambush could have been set up at a better location (i.e., at the intersection of two roads going to Bombay) with benefit of hindsight cannot be held against A112.	Arguments of Petitioner
107)	Arguments of Petitioner
It is further contended that no evidence establishes that A112 deliberately set up the ambush at one road so as to permit the vehicles carrying arms to take the other road to Bombay.	Arguments of Petitioner
The above submissions are unacceptable.	None
The evidence of PW99 establishes that the setting up of the ambush at the place of choice of A 112 was done deliberately by him.	None
A112 told his subordinates that he has specific information about the particular route and time of landing.	None
A112 also told them about Tiger Memon.	None
A112 further told them that he has specific information that they will go through Purar Phata.	None
A112 called off the vigil at midnight and does not organize the same after 31st.	None
Ex facie it appears that it could have been an error of judgment of the officer.	None
None of the information on record shows the smuggling of arms would be conducted by Tiger Memon the said goods would be transported through Purar Phata and it would be done only on 30th and 31st night.	None
109) From the topography of the area, it is also clear that the vigil at Purar Phata was kept deliberately to provide a safe passage to the smugglers pic As rightly pointed out by the prosecution, from the aforesaid topography, it is clear that the ambush could have been kept at the junction as suggested by PW99 which could have covered both the routes to Bombay.	None
The materials clearly show that A112 knowingly directed Nakabandi at Purar Phata and Behar Phata which left SaiMorba Road route open for the smugglers to travel safely.	None
It is also brought to our notice that A112 also spread rumour of a specific information when there was none.	None
It is also not clear as to why the vigil was called off at midnight when as a matter of practice smuggling takes place after midnight.	None
It is also not clear why no vigil was kept after 31st night of January, 1993.	None
All the aforesaid was justified on the basis of nonexistence of specific information.	None
The above said conduct of A112 has to be considered in the light of the fact that A112 was duly informed by his superior that they have intelligence that ISI may send weapons along with silver or gold.	None
The said information requested the Officer to be alert.	None
It is also to be seen that the information of the above said landing was the first such information after the alert notice of 25.01.1993.	None
The said information, amongst others, has been proved by PW470.	None
Deposition of SR Bharadwaj (PW470) PW470 was working as Collector of Customs (Preventive) at Bombay.	None
From his testimony, the following facts emerge He was the senior officer and A112 was working under him.	None
ii)	None
On 24/25.01.1993, he received information from DRI that some ISI syndicate located in MiddleEast may try to smuggle contraband items into India.	None
He told A112 and A102 about this information.	None
A112 told him in the end of January that there was no landing of contraband since either the information was leaked or the movement of customs officials was known.	None
PW470 told A112 to ask the local officers to keep the track of the said information.	None
A perusal of deposition of PW470 establishes that he asked A112 to ask local officers to keep track of the said information and further he had issued a letter being Exhibit No. 1536 informing Mr. R.K. Singh (A102) about landing of large quantity of automatic weapons in next 1530 days.	None
This letter was copied to A112 also.	None
The evidence of PW470 has to be considered in the light of the conduct of A112, emerging from the evidence of PW98 and PW99.	None
Deposition of Bhaskar Krishanji Naik (PW168) PW168 was working as a Superintendent, Customs (Marine and Preventive) Wing since 28.12.1992, in Central Intelligence Unit (C.I.U.) at Everest House, Bombay.	None

Singh and which was also forwarded to A112 stating that large quantity of automatic weapons along with contraband items like gold and silver were likely to land around Bombay in the next 1520 days, and therefore, necessary action should be taken.	None
The deposition of this witness proves that A112 had been informed well in advance that landing of arms was going to take place and it could happen anytime within 1520 days from the time the letter was written, i.e., 25.01.1993.	None
Inspite of clear information that large quantity of automatic weapons will land in next 15 days, A112 only kept ambush for 2 days and that too at wrong places and also spread a rumour that the place was appropriate, since he has a specific information.	None
Deposition of Vishwambhal M. Doiphode (PW171) PW171 was Additional Collector of Customs (Rummaging and Intelligence) Bombay.	None
From his testimony, the following facts emerge He knew A112 as he was also working under the Collector of Custom (Preventive), Shri S.K. Bharadwaj (PW470).	None
The word Panther is used to denote Additional Collector.	None
iii)	None
On the night of 01.02.1993, he received a call at about 2 a.m. from his sources informing him that landing of contraband was taking place at Mhasla.	None

A112, thereafter, gave an alert message to Mhasla, Bankot and Alibaug divisions.	None
It is pointed out by the prosecution that deposition of PW171 clearly establishes that A112 alerted the customs officials at Bankot and Alibaug also whereas the information received was for landing at Mhasla only.	None
It is argued on the side of the CBI that the paper work of giving alert was done by A112 since the message was given by an Additional Collector and something was to be shown to have been done.	Arguments of Respondent
Exhibit 2594  	Arguments of Respondent
X 711 is the VHF Radio logbook.	Arguments of Respondent
The relevant extract of message reads as under Something has happened at Bankot therefore maximum alert to be kept at D31 division starting immediately It shows that A112 had asked to keep a strict vigil at Bankot in the face of clear and specific information that the landing was to take place at Mhasla.	None
The said specific information was distorted as well as converted into a vague message that something is happening in the Alibaug division which is a very big division.	None
In view of the specific information given by a senior officer, the message circulated by A112 about Bankot was completely misleading since Bankot is about 45 kms.	None
from Mhasla.	None
Deposition of Liladhar Dattaray Mhatre (PW172) PW172 was an Officer in Central Excise Department in Bombay.	None
From his testimony, the following facts emerge He received information on 29.01.1993 from his sources that landing of silver was to take place at Shekhadi on 29/31.01.1993.	None
He immediately told A112 about this information.	None
PW172 received information after about 78 days (around 5th or 6th February) that instead of silver, landing of some chemical had taken place on 03.02.1993 at Shekhadi.	None
He told A112 about this information and A112 said kya ho sakta hai?	None
(what can be done) and in cross PW172 says Acha thik hai, main dekhta huin kya hoga (let me see what can be done).	None
The conduct of A112 has to be considered in the light of the letter dated 25.01.1993 proved by PW470.	None
It may also be considered that the second landing could have been obstructed, if immediate action on the said letter was taken.	None
Even the said arms and ammunitions which landed on 03.02.1993 could have been traced, if the said information was shared with the Customs Department as well as the Police.	None
The appellant not only avoided alerting the Department, but also did not share the said piece of information till 25.03.1993 with the Department.	None
It has been contended by learned senior counsel for A112 that he was surprised to hear about the landing of chemicals instead of silver and thus it can be inferred that A112 was not aware of the landing of RDX at Shekhadi.	None
As per the letter issued by PW470, the information was specific that automatic weapons were to land in next 1520 days near Bombay.	None
Inspite of this clear information, A112 only kept ambush for two days and told the officers on duty that he will issue directions, if further ambush is required.	None
We are also satisfied that A112 deliberately did not keep a vigil at the required place and even after the information the chemical had landed and he did not take any steps to further pass on the information until 25.03.1993.	None
It may also be seen in the light of his conduct of diverting attention of the Department from Mhasla to Bankot despite there being specific information from a senior officer of landing on 1st/2nd of February.	None
Deposition of Vivek Vishwanath Kadam (PW163) PW163 was Inspector of Customs, Marine Preventive.	None
From his testimony, the following fact emerges A112, in a meeting of Customs officials told S.K. Bharadwaj (PW470) and other officers present that 60 drums of liquid chemicals had landed somewhere at the coast.	None
The meeting took place on 25.03.1993.	None
A112 did not tell in the meeting that he had received the information of landing that took place on 03.02.1993 on the next day itself.	None
A112 did not disclose that he had information about the landing any time before 25.03.1993.	None
The above evidence proves that A112 had information about the landing that took place on 03.02.1993 however, he chose not to share it with the other officers.	None
Deposition of Prabhakar Natarajan (PW152) PW152 was an Inspector of Customs at Shrivardhan Post.	None
From his testimony, the following facts emerge On 25.03.1993, a meeting was called by the Collector of Customs at the Customs Office at Murud where A112 remarked that a landing of chemicals might have taken place at Shekhadi during the first week of February.	None
Until the said date, i.e. 25.03.1993, S.N. Thapa had not taken any action regarding any landing of RDX which was said to have taken place at Shekhadi on 03.02.1993.	None
A112 did not tell the other officers in the meeting that he had information about the landing.	None
Deposition of Saryuprasad Ramnivaj Maurya (PW100) PW100 was working in the Customs Office, Shrivardhan as an O.T.C. (Operator Tele Communication).	None
His duty was to send and receive wireless messages.	None
He deposed as under He deposed that the record of message received and sent on wireless is maintained by recording the same in VHF Wireless log book.	None
He was shown the VHF radio log book for a period from 11.11.1992 to 06.04.1993	None
He proved Exh.	None
No. 534 (Box No. 17) in court which is the VHF Radio log for 02.02.1993.	None
This message was received from Bombay by Additional Collector of Customs.	None
A112 was the then Additional Collector of Customs in Bombay.	None
The entry of 02.02.1993 was marked as Exh.	None
No. 534A. Panther word is wireless code for Additional Collector (i.e. A112).	None
In view of the above, the following facts emerge A112 was fully aware of the information that the weapons of mass destruction may be smuggled to India along with silver and gold He kept vigil at a place which leaves room for the smugglers to escape from another route to Bombay under the guise of specific information He failed to produce any such specific information ever A112 told that he has specific information that Tiger Memon is going to come through that route in a particular manner Actually, there was no specific information that the smuggler was Tiger Memon and that he was to pass through a particular route The onus was on the accused to prove his specific information for a particular course of conduct undertaken by him	None
He also spread rumour of specific information to mislead and misguide the Department so as to help the smugglers He misdirected the Department by distorting a specific message of landing at Mhasla to be something happening at Bankot about 45 kilometers away from Mahasla, particularly, when the said information came from a senior officer of the Department He failed to explain as to why he did that He further failed to take account of what was done pursuant to the said information He did not do anything on specific information that along with Silver some chemicals have arrived at Shekhadi on 03.02.1993 and Any timely action on the part of A112 could have traced the smuggled goods.	None
The said action could have prevented second landing that took place subsequently.	None
All the above said circumstances cumulatively establish the charges framed against A112 at the trial.	None
The said circumstances leave no room for any alternative hypothesis.	None
We are also satisfied that pursuant to a conspiracy with Tiger Memon and his other coconspirators, A112 misused his official position in order to knowingly facilitate the terrorist act.	None
Under these circumstances, we are satisfied that the prosecution has established the guilt against the appellant and the Designated Court has rightly convicted him and sentenced him.	Decision
Since he died during the pendency of this appeal, there cannot be any direction except confirming the decision of the Designated Court and clarifying the position.	Decision
The appeal is disposed of accordingly.	None
Criminal Appeal No. 1440 of 2007 Muzammil Umar Kadri (A25) Appellant(s) vs. The State of Maharashtra through CBISTF, Mumbai Respondent(s) AND Criminal Appeal No. 1028 of 2012 The State of Maharashtra through CBISTF, Mumbai Appellant(s) vs. Muzammil Umar Kadri (A25) Respondent(s) Heard Mr. Mushtaq Ahmad, learned counsel for the appellant (A25) and Mr. Mukul Gupta, learned senior counsel duly assisted by Mr. Satyakam, learned counsel for the CBI.	None
Criminal Appeal No. 1440 of 2007 is directed against the final judgment and order of conviction and sentence dated 16.10.2006 and 30.05.2007 respectively, whereby the appellant (A25) has been convicted and sentenced to rigorous imprisonment (RI) for life by the Designated Court under TADA for the Bombay Bomb Blast Case, Greater Bombay in B.B.C. No.1/1993.	Issue
Criminal Appeal No. 1028 of 2012 is filed by the CBI against the acquittal of A25 insofar as the charge framed at head firstly, i.e., Conspiracy.	Issue
For convenience, henceforth, we will refer accused (A25) as the appellant.	Issue
Charges A common charge of conspiracy was framed against all the co conspirators including the appellant (A25).	Facts
The material part of the said charge is reproduced herein During the period from December, 1992 to April, 1993 at various places in Bombay, District Raigad and District Thane in India and outside India in Dubai (U.A.E.) and Pakistan, entered into a criminal conspiracy and or were members of the said criminal conspiracy whose object was to commit terrorist acts in India and that you all agreed to commit following illegal acts, namely, to commit terrorist acts with an intent to overawe the Government as by law established, to strike terror in the people, to alienate sections of the people and to adversely affect the harmony amongst different sections of the people, i.e. Hindus and Muslims by using bombs, dynamites, hand grenades and other explosive substances like RDX or inflammable substances or fire arms like AK56 rifles, carbines, pistols and other lethal weapons, in such a manner as to cause or as likely to cause death of or injuries to any person or persons, loss of or damage to and disruption of supplies of services essential to the life of the community, and to achieve the objectives of the conspiracy, you all agreed to smuggle firearms, ammunitions, detonators, hand grenades and high explosives like RDX into India and to distribute the same amongst yourselves and your men of confidence for the purpose of committing terrorist acts and for the said purpose to conceal and store all these arms, ammunitions and explosives at such safe places and amongst yourselves and with your men of confidence till its use for committing terrorist acts and achieving the objects of criminal conspiracy and to dispose off the same as need arises.	Facts
To organize training camps in Pakistan and in India to import and undergo weapons training in handling of arms, ammunitions and explosives to commit terrorist acts.	Facts
To harbour and conceal terrorists coconspirators, and also to aid, abet and knowingly facilitate the terrorist acts and or any act preparatory to the commission of terrorist acts and to render any assistance financial or otherwise for accomplishing the object of the conspiracy to commit terrorist acts, to do and commit any other illegal acts as were necessary for achieving the aforesaid objectives of the criminal conspiracy and that on 12.03.1993 were successful in causing bomb explosions at Stock Exchange Building, Air India Building, Hotel Sea Rock at Bandra, Hotel Centaur at Juhu, Hotel Centaur at Santacruz, Zaveri Bazaar, Katha Bazaar, Century Bazaar at Worli, Petrol Pump adjoining Shiv Sena Bhavan, Plaza Theatre and in lobbing handgrenades at Macchimar Hindu Colony, Mahim and at Bay52, Sahar International Airport which left more than 257 persons dead, 713 injured and property worth about Rs.27 crores destroyed, and attempted to cause bomb explosions at Naigaum Cross Road and Dhanji Street, all in the city of Bombay and its suburbs i.e. within Greater Bombay.	Facts
And thereby committed offences punishable under Section 3(3) of TADA (P) Act, 1987 and Section 120B of IPC read with Sections 3(2)(i)(ii), 3(3)(4), 5 and 6 of TADA (P) Act, 1987 and read with Sections 302, 307, 326, 324, 427, 435, 436, 201 and 212 of Indian Penal Code and offences under Sections 3 and 7 read with Sections 25 (1A), (1B)(a) of the Arms Act, 1959, Sections 9B (1)(a)(b)(c) of the Explosives Act, 1884, Sections 3, 4(a)(b), 5 and 6 of the Explosive Substances Act, 1908 and Section 4 of the Prevention of Damage to Public Property Act, 1984 and within my cognizance.	Facts
In addition to the aforesaid principal charge of conspiracy, the appellant (A25) was also charged on other counts which are summarized as under At head Secondly He committed an offence punishable under Section 3(3) of TADA by participating in the landing and transportation of smuggled arms, ammunitions and explosives at Shekhadi for the purpose of committing terrorist acts.	None
At head Thirdly In or around January 1993, with intent to aid terrorists, he possessed 16 AK56 rifles and 26 magazines in contravention of the provisions of the Arms Act, 1959 and the Arms Rules, 1962 and thereby committed an offence punishable under Section 6 of TADA.	None
At head	None
Fourthly	None
By possessing the aforementioned rifles and magazines, he committed an offence punishable under Section 3 and Section 7 read with Sections 25(1A) and 25 (1B)(a) of the Arms Act, 1959.	None
Conviction Sentence	None
The appellant has been convicted and sentenced for the above said charges as under The appellant has been convicted for the offence of conspiracy under Section 3(3) of TADA read with Section 120B of IPC read with the offences described at head firstly and sentenced to RI for life along with a fine of Rs. 50,000/, in default, to further undergo RI for 1 year.	Facts
(charge firstly)	None
The appellant has also been convicted for the offence under Section 3(3) of TADA and sentenced to RI for 10 years along with a fine of Rs. 25,000/, in default, to further undergo RI for 6 months.	Facts
(charge secondly) (ii) The appellant has also been convicted for the offence under Section 6 of TADA and sentenced to RI for 14 years along with a fine of Rs. 50,000/, in default, to further undergo RI for 1 year.	Facts
(charge thirdly) (iii)	Facts
The appellant has also been convicted for the offences punishable under Section 3 and Section 7 read with Sections 25(1A) and 25(1 B)(a) of the Arms Act, 1959 but no separate sentence was awarded on the said count.	None
(charge fourthly)	None
Mr. Mushtaq Ahmad, learned counsel for the appellant (A25), after taking us through the relevant materials relied on by the prosecution, submitted that firstly his own confession is not voluntary and not genuine and, in any event, he retracted the same, hence, the conviction based on his confession is not sustainable.	Arguments of Petitioner
He also submitted that though the prosecution has relied on confessional statement of coaccused, particularly, Dawood Dawood Taklya Mohd.	Arguments of Petitioner
Phanse Phanasmiyan (A14), Khalil Ahmed Syed Ali Nazir (A42) and Sujjad Alam Iqbal Abdul Hakim Nazir (A61), they have not attributed to any specific role of the appellant A25.	Arguments of Petitioner
He further submitted that the recoveries alleged to have been made by the prosecution are not acceptable and, in any event, it contained several infirmities.	Arguments of Petitioner
Learned counsel appearing for the CBI refuted all the above contentions and after basing reliance on oral and documentary evidence submitted that the prosecution has established the charges leveled against the appellant and the Designated Court has rightly convicted and sentenced him for life.	None
Evidence The evidence against the appellant (A25) is in the form of i) his own confession confessions made by other coconspirators (coaccused) testimony of prosecution witnesses and documentary evidence.	None
Confessional Statement of Muzammil Umar Kadri (A25)	None
The prosecution projected that the involvement of the appellant (A 25) in the conspiracy is evident from his own confession recorded under Section 15 of TADA on 17.04.1993 (1400 hrs.)	None
and 20.04.1993 (1200 hrs.)	Reasoning
by Shri Sanjay Pandey (PW492), the then DCP, ZoneVIII, Bombay.	Reasoning
It is seen that except the appellant, the recording officer (PW492) asked all the persons to leave the Chamber and there was no one who could hear and see the proceedings of the same.	None
Thereafter, PW492 apprised about himself and also ascertained whether he has any complaint against the police and also informed him that he is not bound to make a statement and if such a statement is made, the same can be used against him.	None
He also ascertained whether any police official or any other person threatened him to make a statement etc.	None
After apprising all the formalities and after satisfying himself that the accused is willing to make a statement voluntarily, he directed the officer concerned for production of the accused on 19.04.1993 after expiry of 48 hours.	None
It is further seen that he was produced on 20.04.1993 by API Gaikwad.	None
Again, after putting several questions to ascertain his willingness and genuineness, PW492 recorded his statement.	None
Though learned counsel for the appellant submitted that he was forced to make such a statement, a perusal of the entire proceedings clearly show that the officer, who recorded the confession, followed the procedure strictly and recorded his statement after satisfying himself that the accused is giving confession voluntarily without any pressure from any corner.	None
We were taken through the entire confession of the appellant.	None
The confession of appellant (A25) is summarized below At the relevant time, he was an autorickshaw driver.	None
He was a resident of Mhasla and became acquainted with Dawood Taklya (A14) who also lived in the same locality.	None
He knew that Taklya was involved in the landing of smuggled goods.	None
He also knew that Rahim Laundrywala (deceased accused) and Sharif Abdul Gafoor Parkar Dadabhai (A17) were the partners of Dawood Taklya in the aforesaid activities.	None
In or around MarchApril 1992, he was taken by Dawood Taklya to Shekhadi for unloading of smuggled silver and its transportation to a Tower, at which time, he saw Tiger Memon, Anwar and Shafi (AA).	None
The silver was smuggled by Tiger Memon.	None
He was paid Rs. 1,200/ by Dawood Taklya for the said assignment.	None
Again, in August, 1992, he was taken by Dawood Taklya to Shekhadi for unloading of smuggled silver and its transportation to Waghani Tower, at which time, Rahim Laundrywala and A17 were also present.	None
He was paid Rs. 1,500/ by Dawood Taklya.	None
The silver was smuggled by Tiger Memon.	None
In January, 1993, he was called at the residence of Khalil Ahmed Sayed Ali Nasir (A42) by Rahim Laundrywala and Shafi and was asked to keep 16 rifles and 32 cassettes at his residence, which he kept with him.	None
On 03.02.1993, he escorted the truck carrying the smuggled consignment from Borli to Waghani Tower where he saw Tiger Memon, Dawood Taklya, A17, Anwar, Shafi and others.	None
On 07.02.1993, Dawood had taken the appellant to Shekhadi in the rickshaw of Sajjad Alam Iqbal Abdul Hakim Nazir (A61) since the appellant had already sold his rickshaw.	None
On 07.02.1993, at about 11.30 a.m., Dawood Taklya had come to his house in the rickshaw of A61 and took 3 rifles and 6 magazines out of the 16 rifles and 32 magazines which were kept at his house and told that the message was received from Tiger Memon regarding the same.	None
Thereafter, Dawood Taklya also took him in the rickshaw of A61 to Shekhadi and they reached Shekhadi at about 9.00 p.m.	None
Thereafter, Sajjad Alam was told to go to the Tower in the rickshaw and the appellant was asked to get down at Mehendadi.	None
Mr. Mushtaq Ahmad, learned counsel for the appellant, by drawing our attention to Exh. 1654 (Hindi version of his confession) pointed out that there are certain overlappings and corrections, hence, in the absence of any explanation, the same cannot be used against him.	Arguments of Petitioner
In the light of the said contention, we have carefully verified the translated version in English.	Arguments of Petitioner
We find no substance in the said contention.	None
On the other hand, at several places, A25 conveyed his desire to make a statement and at the end he informed the officer, who recorded the statement, that he understood everything and the entire recorded statement is true and acceptable.	None
In such circumstances, we are unable to accept the stand taken by the appellant.	None
However, though the very same appellant had retracted his confession but the same was done only on 03.10.1993, i.e., after a gap of nearly about 6 months.	None
In the absence of any proper explanation for not retracting immediately after making such a statement, even though he appeared before the Magistrate senior officers on several occasions, the fact remains that he had not retracted.	None
Even otherwise, as observed in the earlier part of our judgment, a perusal of the retracted statement shows that the same was prepared by someone and he merely signed the same.	None
The panchnama dated 26.03.1993 was prepared in Marathi with regard to recoveries made from A25.	Arguments of Petitioner
The English translation of the same was also placed on record.	Arguments of Petitioner
Learned counsel for the appellant has pointed out that out of 2 panch witnesses, namely, Mr. Walmik Shankar Gite and Mr. Laxman Loku Karkera, the prosecution has examined Mr. Walmik Shankar Gite only.	Arguments of Petitioner
According to the counsel, he is a resident of Bombay and he was taken by the police to a place which is at a distance of 250 km.	None
The said Panchnama recorded details of arms and ammunitions seized from the house of the appellant.	None
Learned counsel has also pointed out some discrepancy in the signature of panch witnesses.	None
We also verified the xerox copy of the Panchnama dated 26.03.1993 and we do not find any glaring discrepancy as pointed out by the counsel.	None
A perusal of the above confession of A25 shows that he was willingly involved in the landing of smuggled arms and ammunitions at Shekhadi and that he also possessed and stored arms and ammunitions at the instructions of Tiger Memon.	None
We are also satisfied that the A25 has made the above confession voluntarily, without any pressure or coercion and the same has been recorded after following all the safeguards enumerated under Section 15 of TADA and the rules framed thereunder.	None
Confessional Statements of coaccused Apart from his own confession, the involvement of the appellant (A 25) has also been disclosed in the confessional statements of three other coaccused.	Reasoning
The legality and acceptability of the confessions of the co accused has already been considered by us in the earlier part of our discussion.	None
The said confessions insofar as they refer to the appellant (A 25) are summarized hereinbelow Confessional Statement of Dawood Dawood Taklya Mohd.	None
Phanse Phanasmiyan (A14)	None
Confessional statement of A14 under Section 15 of TADA was recorded on 15.04.1993 (1755 hrs.)	Reasoning
and 17.04.1993 (1930 hrs.)	Reasoning
by Shri Krishan Lal Bishnoi (PW193), the then DCP, Zone III, Bombay.	Reasoning
The said confession reveals as under His son, Sarfaraj informed him that Shafi had kept the weapons at the appellants house.	None
The appellant was present at the time of the first landing at Shekhadi.	None
The appellant alongwith Iqbal and A42 patrolled the car in which Tiger and others (including A14) were travelling when they were on their way to Waghani Tower alongwith the truck which was loaded with arms and ammunitions that had landed at Shekhadi.	None
The appellant was present when the arms and ammunitions were unloaded from the truck at Waghani Tower.	None
At the instance of Tiger and his men, he went to the residence of the appellant to get 3 rifles and 6 magazines which were kept at his house and later on gave the same to Tiger.	None
The appellant was present at the time of the second landing at Shekhadi and after completion of the landing operation, A14 returned home alongwith the appellant and others.	None
A14 paid Rs. 4,000/ to the appellant for the work done during the landing operation.	None
The above statement of A14 makes clear the relationship of A25 with Tiger and his men and his participation in landing and transportation of arms as well as keeping of arms in his house as directed by Tiger and taking of arms from his house.	None
Confessional Statement of Khalil Ahmed Syed Ali Nazir (A42)	None
Confessional statement of A42 under Section 15 of TADA was recorded on 16.04.1993 (2030 hrs.)	Reasoning
and 19.04.1993 (2100 hrs.)	Reasoning
by Mr. P.D. Pawar (PW185), the then DCP, Zone V, Bombay.	Reasoning
The said confession reveals that on the night of 03.03.1993, the appellant, alongwith others, was sitting in the truck and after reaching Shekhadi, the smuggled material was loaded in the said truck.	None
Confessional Statement of Sujjad Alam Iqbal Abdul Hakim Nazir (A61)	None
Confessional statement of A61 under Section 15 of TADA was recorded on 19.04.1993 (1140 hrs.)	Reasoning
and 21.04.1993 (1050 hrs.)	Reasoning
by Shri Krishan Lal Bishnoi (PW193), the then DCP, Zone III, Bombay.	Reasoning
The said confession reveals as under The appellant was the man of Tiger and was present at the residence of A42 in the evening of 20.01.1993.	None
Shafi was also present there and they were unloading some goods from a gunny bag in a jeep.	None
At that time, Sarfaraj (Dawood Taklyas son) was also present.	None
After opening the gunny bags, A61 saw 16 rifles and 32 magazines in it.	None
Thereafter, A61, A42 and the appellant took the above rifles and magazines in an autorickshaw to the his (A25) residence.	None
The appellant was present at Waghani Tower during the first landing at Shekhadi.	None
On 09.02.1993, A61 alongwith A14 and A42 went to the appellants residence.	None
A14 told the appellant to hand over 3 rifles and 6 cassettes to him.	None
Accordingly, the appellant handed over the same in a gunny bag which was later on collected by Tiger Memon from Lone Phata.	None
The appellant also accompanied A61 and others while going to Shekhadi for the second landing.	None
A perusal of the confessional statements of all the above three accused persons, namely, A14, A42 and A61 establish the fact that it corroborates with the confessional statement of A25 in material particulars.	Reasoning
The involvement of the appellant is established inasmuch as The appellant kept 16 rifles and 32 cassettes at his residence at the instance of Shafi.	None
The appellant participated and assisted in both the landings of arms and ammunitions at Shekhadi.	None
The appellant was also involved in the transportation of smuggled consignment of weapons from Worli to Waghani Tower.	None
On 09.02.1993, A14 had come to his house to take 3 rifles and 6 magazines at the behest of Tiger Memon.	None
Deposition of Prosecution Witnesses Apart from the aforesaid evidence, the involvement and the role of the appellant in the conspiracy, as stated above, is disclosed by the deposition of various prosecution witnesses which are as under Deposition of Laxman Karkera (PW45) PW45 revealed as under On 26.03.1993, he acted as a panch witness and, on the said day, the appellant led the panchas and the police to his (A25) house near Urdu school in village Mehandadi .	None
While conducting a search in his house, the police found 3 gunny bags that were buried three feet deep in a half constructed bathroom.	None
When the gunny bags were opened by the police, the same were found to be containing 13 AK56 rifles and 26 empty magazines of AK56 rifles.	None
The rifles and magazines were examined by the police and the magazines could be fitted into the cavity of the said rifles.	None
The Police then took charge of the rifles and magazines and the labels of signatures of PW45 and others were pasted on each AK56 rifle and magazine.	None
Then, the same were wrapped in a paper and were labeled and sealed and signatures of PW45 and others were obtained on the same.	None
The police also took charge of the 3 gunny bags.	None
All the above events were recorded by one police officer in a Panchnama and the same was signed by PI Pawar, PW45 and the copanch.	None
The panchanama Exh. 158 was read over to PW45 and the copanch and was found to be correctly drawn.	None
He has correctly identified the Panchanama.	None
He has also correctly identified PI Pawar as the one who had signed the said panchanama and PSI Nerlekar as the one who had written the said panchanama.	None
The rifles, magazines and 3 gunny bags seized by the police, as stated above, were duly identified by him in the court.	None
Deposition of HB Pawar (PW596) PW596 revealed as under As instructed by DCP Shri Rakesh Maria, he went alongwith other police officers and staff to Mhasala on 26.03.1993.	None
After receiving information from a person, A14 was arrested by him in Buddha Wada locality of Mhasala.	None
After interrogation, A14 led PSI Rane, PW596 and others to Mhendadi village and they arrested the appellant and A42 from the chowk of the said village.	None
Thereafter, he interrogated both the said accused and decided to search their houses.	None
One	None
Shri Laxman Karkera (PW45) agreed to act as a panch witness.	None
Thereafter, the panch witnesses and the police party along with the appellant went to his house near an Urdu School of the said village.	None
The said house was shown to them by the appellant himself.	None
The search of the said house was taken in the presence of the panch witnesses.	None
3 gunny bags were found to be concealed about 3 feet deep under the tiles of a bathroom.	None
The said 3 gunny bags were opened and were found to be containing 13 AK56 rifles and 26 empty magazines of AK56 rifles.	None
Thereafter, each of the AK56 rifles was wrapped in a brown paper and the said packet was tied by means of a string and labels of signatures of panch witnesses and his signature was affixed on each of the packet and the same were also sealed by using the lac seal and in the same manner the 26 empty magazines and the said 3 gunny bags were also wrapped in a brown paper and labelled and sealed.	None
He recorded the description of the rifles and magazines in a panchanama by dictating the matter to PSI Nerlekar.	None
He also took charge of the rifles, magazines and gunny bags.	None
The panchanama was read over to the panch witnesses and their signatures were obtained to ensure its correctness.	None
He also countersigned the same.	None
The above depositions of PW45 and PW596, corroborate with the confession of the appellant and those of the 3 coaccused persons mentioned above and unmistakably establish the possession of the contraband material by the appellant within a notified area.	None
Even lengthy crossexamination of the above witnesses has failed to destroy their testimonies.	None
The recovered articles were sent to FSL for opinion by Waman Kulkarni (PW662) vide Exh. 2440 and a positive FSL Report Exh. 2440A was received by the Police.	None
Apart from the evidence of Police Inspector, i.e., PW596, PW588, PW 605 and PW606, the abovesaid confessional statements of A14, A42 and A 61 prove the prosecution case with reference to the role of A25 in handling and transporting arms and ammunitions from Shekhadi port to various places and it is also clear that arms were stored in his house and taken to the place as directed by the Tiger.	None
We have already highlighted the Panchnama containing all the details of arms and ammunitions collected from the residence of A25.	None
PW45 explained all those details and he admitted the said Panchnama as well as his signature therein.	None
Though A25 was represented by a counsel before the trial Court, there was no crossexamination at all.	None
Taking note of all the above materials, the Designated Court, after analyzing the same, came to the conclusion that the material contained in the confession of A25 clearly reveals his involvement in landing at Shekhadi and its transportation.	None
The corroborative material contained in the confession of A25 i.e. his involvement in landing at Shekhadi and its transportation, for which he was charged with, has also been proved in the confessions of A14, A42 and A61.	None
Considering the role played by him i.e., he was possessing such a large number of arms and ammunitions after the Shekhadi operation was over and was holding the same for a considerable period, the same also denotes that he was a man of close confidence of prime accused persons.	None
The Designated Court also rightly concluded that the act committed by him was for furthering the object of conspiracy and he himself having committed the same during the 1st half of February, 1993 i.e. much prior to even Tiger Memon fixing the target for committing serial bomb blasts in Bombay and is guilty for the offence of conspiracy to commit terrorist acts punishable under Section 3(3) of TADA.	None
In view of the evidence discussed above, we hold that the appellant was actively involved in the conspiracy to cause blasts in Bombay and in consequence of the said involvement, he has committed the offences for which he has been charged and we affirm the same.	Decision
As rightly pointed out by the prosecution, the facts and events stated by the appellant in his own confession are duly corroborated by the confessions of other coaccused, thereby clearly revealing his involvement in the landings at Shekhadi and that he was unauthorisedly in possession of the contraband material.	None
Therefore, the appellant is guilty for the offences for which he has been charged from head firstly to fourthly.	None
Appeal filed by the State of Maharashtra through CBI Criminal Appeal No. 1028 of 2012 Insofar as the appeal filed by the CBI against acquittal of the appellant (A25) for the charge mentioned at head firstly, viz., conspiracy is concerned, in view of the fact that the appellant (A25) has already been convicted for the same and sentenced to RI for life, learned senior counsel for the CBI has not pressed the appeal before this Court, hence, we are of the view that there is no need to consider this appeal in view of the reason appended above and therefore, the appeal is liable to be dismissed.	None
Sentence Regarding sentence, the prosecution submitted that the appellant was given full opportunity to defend himself on the question of quantum of sentence.	Arguments of Respondent
His statement was recorded on 17.10.2006 (Exh.2984) in which he prayed that the following factors, amongst others, may be considered while determining his sentence He is the sole bread winner of his family comprising of his wife and three small children and ii)	None
His wife is suffering from a mental ailment.	None
With respect to the above contentions regarding quantum of sentence, the prosecution submitted that the appellant was in possession and storage of 13 AK56 rifles and 26 magazines for a considerable period of time.	Arguments of Respondent
From the materials, it is clear that the appellant neither dissociated himself nor resisted from participating in the landings at Shekhadi or transportation of contraband material to Waghani Tower nor did he inform the same to the police authorities or took any steps for the same.	None
This is sufficient to show that he was responsible for the blasts in Bombay and he was very well aware of its consequences.	None
In view of the above, we are of the view that the sentence awarded by the Designated Court to the appellant is justified and the same is confirmed.	Decision
Consequently, the appeal is dismissed.	Decision
Criminal Appeal No. 1441 of 2007 Vijay Krishnaji Patil (A116) Appellant(s) vs. The State of Maharashtra, through Superintendent of Police, CBI (STF), Mumbai .	None
Respondent(s)	None
Mr. Chander Uday Singh, learned senior counsel appeared for the appellant (A116) and Mr. Mukul Gupta, learned senior counsel duly assisted by Mr. Satyakam, learned counsel for the respondentCBI.	None
The present appeal is directed against the final judgment and order of conviction and sentence dated 26.09.2006 and 22.05.2007 respectively whereby the appellant (A116) has been convicted and sentenced to rigorous imprisonment (RI) for life by the Designated Court under TADA for the Bombay Bomb Blast Case, Greater Bombay in B.B.C. No.1/1993.	Issue
Charges A common charge of conspiracy was framed against all the co conspirators including the appellant (A116).	Facts
The relevant portion of the said charge is reproduced hereunder During the period from December, 1992 to April, 1993 at various places in Bombay, District Raigad and District Thane in India and outside India in Dubai (U.A.E.) and Pakistan, entered into a criminal conspiracy and or were members of the said criminal conspiracy whose object was to commit terrorist acts in India and that you all agreed to commit following illegal acts, namely, to commit terrorist acts with an intent to overawe the Government as by law established, to strike terror in the people, to alienate sections of the people and to adversely affect the harmony amongst different sections of the people, i.e. Hindus and Muslims by using bombs, dynamites, hand grenades and other explosive substances like RDX or inflammable substances or fire arms like AK56 rifles, carbines, pistols and other lethal weapons, in such a manner as to cause or as likely to cause death of or injuries to any person or persons, loss of or damage to and disruption of supplies of services essential to the life of the community, and to achieve the objectives of the conspiracy, you all agreed to smuggle firearms, ammunitions, detonators, hand grenades and high explosives like RDX into India and to distribute the same amongst yourselves and your men of confidence for the purpose of committing terrorist acts and for the said purpose to conceal and store all these arms, ammunitions and explosives at such safe places and amongst yourselves and with your men of confidence till its use for committing terrorist acts and achieving the objects of criminal conspiracy and to dispose off the same as need arises.	Facts
To organize training camps in Pakistan and in India to import and undergo weapons training in handling of arms, ammunitions and explosives to commit terrorist acts.	Facts
To harbour and conceal terrorists coconspirators, and also to aid, abet and knowingly facilitate the terrorist acts and or any act preparatory to the commission of terrorist acts and to render any assistance financial or otherwise for accomplishing the object of the conspiracy to commit terrorist acts, to do and commit any other illegal acts as were necessary for achieving the aforesaid objectives of the criminal conspiracy and that on 12.03.1993 were successful in causing bomb explosions at Stock Exchange Building, Air India Building, Hotel Sea Rock at Bandra, Hotel Centaur at Juhu, Hotel Centaur at Santacruz, Zaveri Bazaar, Katha Bazaar, Century Bazaar at Worli, Petrol Pump adjoining Shiv Sena Bhavan, Plaza Theatre and in lobbing handgrenades at Macchimar Hindu Colony, Mahim and at Bay52, Sahar International Airport which left more than 257 persons dead, 713 injured and property worth about Rs.27 crores destroyed, and attempted to cause bomb explosions at Naigaum Cross Road and Dhanji Street, all in the city of Bombay and its suburbs i.e. within Greater Bombay.	Facts
And thereby committed offences punishable under Section 3(3) of TADA (P) Act, 1987 and Section 120B of IPC read with Sections 3(2)(i)(ii), 3(3)(4), 5 and 6 of TADA (P) Act, 1987 and read with Sections 302, 307, 326, 324, 427, 435, 436, 201 and 212 of Indian Penal Code and offences under Sections 3 and 7 read with Sections 25 (1A), (1B)(a) of the Arms Act, 1959, Sections 9B (1)(a)(b)(c) of the Explosives Act, 1884, Sections 3, 4(a)(b), 5 and 6 of the Explosive Substances Act, 1908 and Section 4 of the Prevention of Damage to Public Property Act, 1984 and within my cognizance.	Facts
In addition to the abovesaid principal charge of conspiracy, the appellant was also charged on other count which reads as under At head Secondly The appellant, in pursuance of the aforesaid criminal conspiracy, intentionally aided and abetted coaccused persons by allowing them to smuggle into India and transport arms and ammunitions, which were brought into the country for the purpose of committing terrorist acts which were intercepted by a team of Police Officers on the night of 09/01/1993 at Gondghar Phata and allowed to pass the said contraband items in lieu of a bribe of Rs. 7,00,000/ and thereby facilitated the commission of terrorist acts, punishable under section 3(3) of TADA Act, 1987.	Facts
The charges mentioned above were proved against the appellant (A 116).	Facts
The appellant has been convicted and sentenced for the abovesaid charges as under Conviction and Sentence	Facts
The appellant has been convicted for the offence of conspiracy read with the offences described at head firstly and sentenced to RI for life along with a fine of Rs. 1,00,000/, in default, to further undergo RI for 3 years.	Facts
(charge firstly) ii)	Facts
The appellant has also been convicted under Section 3(3) of TADA for commission of offences at head secondly and sentenced to RI for life along with a fine of Rs. 1,00,000/, in default, to further undergo RI for 3 years.	Facts
(charge secondly)	None
Evidence At the time of commission of offence, the appellant (A116) was posted as P.S.I. (Police SubInspector), Police Station, Shrivardhan.	None
The evidence against the appellant (A116) is in the form of confessions made by other coconspirators (coaccused) testimony of prosecution witnesses and documentary evidence.	None
Confessional Statements of coaccused The involvement of the appellant has been disclosed in the confessional statements of the following coaccused.	Reasoning
The legality and acceptability of the confessions of the coaccused has already been considered by us in the earlier part of our discussion.	Reasoning

In his confession, he stated that Rs. 25,000/ was paid to Shrivardhan Police Station for landing on two occasions.	None
Learned senior counsel for the appellant, by pointing out the above confessional statements, particularly, the confession of A30, submitted that the prosecution has not shown or produced any material on record that the police officer was aware of the arms and ammunitions that had landed at Dighi Jetty and that the same were transported along with silver boxes.	Arguments of Petitioner
We have carefully analysed the confessional statements including that of A30 and we find no force in the submission made by learned senior counsel for the appellant.	None
On the other hand, we are unable to accept the said submission.	None
A perusal of the confessional statements of all the above accused, namely, A17, A30, A82, A134 and A136 clearly establish the fact that it corroborates with each other.	Reasoning
After consideration of all the abovesaid confessional statements of the coaccused, the involvement of the appellant in the conspiracy is established inasmuch as The arms and ammunitions had landed at Dighi Jetty in the second week of January, 1993.	None
The landing agents used to talk to the officers of Customs Police Department.	None
The appellant knowingly let off a truck and a tempo carrying smuggled goods pursuant to negotiations on acceptance of bribe of Rs. 8/10 lakhs.	None
As the accused persons were not carrying such a huge amount, the appellant kept 5/8 silver bars as a token for security.	None
The special negotiation and special amount agreed upon shows that the appellant demanded unusual amount in view of the nature of goods smuggled.	None
In other words, he was aware that the consignment was containing arms and ammunitions.	None
The appellant, after consultation with A82, Custom official (who had knowledge that goods could be weapons after the Departmental alert of December, 1992) allowed the trucks loaded with smuggled goods to proceed.	None
The confession of A134 establishes the link between the landing and Mohammed Mustafa Dosa and Dawood Ibrahim and also the landed arms and ammunitions with Tiger Memon.	None
Deposition of Prosecution Witnesses Apart from the aforesaid evidence, the involvement and the role of the appellant in the conspiracy, as stated above, is disclosed by the depositions of various prosecution witnesses which are as under Deposition of Dilip Bhiku Pansare (PW97) PW97 was working as a Mechanic in State Transport Corporation.	None

From the perusal of the above, it is clear that The appellant was well known to the accused persons who referred to him in casual manner.	None
The police party, after checking both the trucks for a considerable period of time had negotiations with the smugglers.	None
(iii) Pursuant to the negotiations, the appellant demanded a sum of Rs. 8/10 lakhs from the smugglers and kept 45 silver bars as a token for security.	None
The keys of the jetty were given to Shabbir (AA) at the instance of the police.	None
The appellant paid Rs. 2,000/ to PW156 which was handed over to him by Mane (A101) for giving keys of the Jetty to Shabbir.	None
It is relevant to mention that the said witness was not even cross examined on behalf of the appellant (A116).	None
Other witnesses Deposition of Yeshwant Govind Kadam (PW109) PW109 is a panch witness and deposed that Panchnama dated 21.04.1993 marked as Exhibit 563 was drawn in his presence.	None
The said Panchnama records that Ramesh Dattatray Mali (A101), Police Constable was given Rs. 15,000/ by A116 in connection with smuggling matter and this money was produced by Mali (A101) in presence of two panchas.	None
The said witness also deposed about the Panchnama dated 22.04.1993 marked as Exhibit 564.	None
The panchnama records that out of the monies taken by A116 in smuggling, he handed over Rs. 25,000/ to P.C. Krishna Tukaram Pingle, B. No. 1499 and that P.C. Pingle was producing the money taken in the Police Station.	None
He further deposed and proved the Panchnama dated 25.04.1993 marked as Exh. 565 which records that Inspector Ashok Narayan Muneshwar (A70) was given Rs. 30,000 in connection with smuggling of goods at Dighi and that he produced the said money in front of panchas.	None
By pointing out the above evidence, learned senior counsel for the appellant, argued that at the most it denotes that at the time of interception, the police found only silver bricks in one truck and similar bricks and some boxes in the other truck.	Arguments of Petitioner
Even after counting, they found 100 silver bricks and some boxes.	Arguments of Petitioner
He further submitted that when the police enquired about the contents of the boxes, Chacha (A136) replied that the boxes contained watches.	Arguments of Petitioner
In other words, according to him, the evidence and the entire materials relied on by the prosecution denote that the police had knowledge of only silver bricks and watches, i.e., the contents of the boxes.	Arguments of Petitioner
Finally, he submitted that the knowledge in furtherance of the act of abetment as contemplated under Section 3(3) of TADA seems to be absent and cannot be inferred on the basis of surmises merely because the appellant was the PSI.	Arguments of Petitioner
In the light of the vehement arguments, we have carefully analysed the prosecution witnesses and the materials placed.	None
Here again, we are unable to concur with the arguments.	None
On the other hand, we are unable to accept the same.	None
On perusal of the entire evidence as placed by the prosecution, the following facts emerge The appellant (A116) arranged for the keys to be given to Shabbir (AA) for the purposes of landing.	None
A police party led by the appellant intercepted two trucks at Gondghar Phata and after checking for a considerable period of time and after negotiating for half an hour, let them off The appellant was well acquainted with the smugglers The appellant had secret negotiations with the smugglers as well as consultation with the Custom official Gurav (A82) for fixing the special bribe amount The appellant took silver bars as security in lieu of cash and kept the same in the house of PW94 who duly corroborates with the fact that he kept the bars in his house The appellant paid Rs. 2,000/ to PW156 for handing over the keys of the Dighi Jetty to Shabbir Kadri (AA) on 09.01.1993 the day when arms and ammunitions landed at Dighi.	None
It may be pointed out here that sufficient evidence has been placed on record by the prosecution to show that part of the consignment which landed at Dighi was also delivered to Tiger Memon.	None
Sentence Coming to sentence, it is not in dispute that the appellant (A116) was the head of the police party.	None
The evidence clearly reveals that the appellant was primarily responsible for the decision arrived at in allowing the said contraband smuggled material to be transported further without the same being intercepted checked by the police in lieu of the bribe amount to be received.	None
Further, the appellant was given full opportunity to defend himself on the question of quantum of sentence.	Arguments of Respondent
The appellant filed statement dated 24.01.2007 on the quantum of sentence which is Exh. 2954.	Facts
The appellant prayed that the following, amongst other factors, may be considered while determining his sentence He was the sole bread winner of his family and He was in the government service.	None
The Designated Court, after considering the factors pleaded by the appellant and the nature of crime committed by him, held as under 499considering the facts that A116 was head of local police and as such was duty bound to make every attempt to prevent commission of a crime, but instead of carrying his duty, he had allowed commission of crime and so also further crimes by allowing transportation of contraband material and having acted in such a manner for receiving a bribe amount makes it extremely difficult to accept submission for leniency.	None
As rightly pointed out by learned senior counsel for the CBI, the crime of the appellant may be considered in the light of the fact that he was the protector of law and he has breached the trust of the people of the country.	None
Had he honestly done his duty, perhaps the whole disaster could have been obviated.	None
In the light of the above, we are of the view that the sentence awarded by the Designated Court to the appellant is justified.	Decision
The above said evidence substantiates and establishes the charge of conspiracy framed against the appellant (A116).	None
We fully agree with the reasoning and ultimate conclusion of the Designated Court both on the conviction and sentence.	None
Consequently, the appeal is liable to be dismissed.	Decision
Criminal Appeal No. 401 of 2008 Mohd.	None
Salim Mira Moiddin Shaikh Salim Kutta (A134) Appellant(s) vs. The State of Maharashtra, through CBISTF, Mumbai Respondent(s)	None
Mr. Chander Uday Singh, learned senior counsel appeared for the appellant (A134) and Mr. Mukul Gupta, learned senior counsel duly assisted by Mr. Satyakam, learned counsel for the respondent (CBI).	None
The instant appeal is directed against the final judgment and order of conviction and sentence dated 19.10.2006 and 05.06.2007 respectively whereby the appellant (A134) has been convicted and sentenced to rigorous imprisonment (RI) for life by the Designated Court under TADA for the Bombay Bomb Blast Case, Greater Bombay in B.B.C. No.1/1993.	Issue
Charges A common charge of conspiracy was framed against all the co conspirators including the appellant herein.	Facts
The relevant portion of the said charge is reproduced hereunder During the period from December, 1992 to April, 1993 at various places in Bombay, District Raigad and District Thane in India and outside India in Dubai (U.A.E.) and Pakistan, entered into a criminal conspiracy and or were members of the said criminal conspiracy whose object was to commit terrorist acts in India and that you all agreed to commit following illegal acts, namely, to commit terrorist acts with an intent to overawe the Government as by law established, to strike terror in the people, to alienate sections of the people and to adversely affect the harmony amongst different sections of the people, i.e. Hindus and Muslims by using bombs, dynamites, hand grenades and other explosive substances like RDX or inflammable substances or fire arms like AK56 rifles, carbines, pistols and other lethal weapons, in such a manner as to cause or as likely to cause death of or injuries to any person or persons, loss of or damage to and disruption of supplies of services essential to the life of the community, and to achieve the objectives of the conspiracy, you all agreed to smuggle firearms, ammunitions, detonators, hand grenades and high explosives like RDX into India and to distribute the same amongst yourselves and your men of confidence for the purpose of committing terrorist acts and for the said purpose to conceal and store all these arms, ammunitions and explosives at such safe places and amongst yourselves and with your men of confidence till its use for committing terrorist acts and achieving the objects of criminal conspiracy and to dispose off the same as need arises.	Facts
To organize training camps in Pakistan and in India to import and undergo weapons training in handling of arms, ammunitions and explosives to commit terrorist acts.	Facts
To harbour and conceal terrorists coconspirators, and also to aid, abet and knowingly facilitate the terrorist acts and or any act preparatory to the commission of terrorist acts and to render any assistance financial or otherwise for accomplishing the object of the conspiracy to commit terrorist acts, to do and commit any other illegal acts as were necessary for achieving the aforesaid objectives of the criminal conspiracy and that on 12.03.1993 were successful in causing bomb explosions at Stock Exchange Building, Air India Building, Hotel Sea Rock at Bandra, Hotel Centaur at Juhu, Hotel Centaur at Santacruz, Zaveri Bazaar, Katha Bazaar, Century Bazaar at Worli, Petrol Pump adjoining Shiv Sena Bhavan, Plaza Theatre and in lobbing handgrenades at Macchimar Hindu Colony, Mahim and at Bay52, Sahar International Airport which left more than 257 persons dead, 713 injured and property worth about Rs.27 crores destroyed, and attempted to cause bomb explosions at Naigaum Cross Road and Dhanji Street, all in the city of Bombay and its suburbs i.e. within Greater Bombay.	Facts
And thereby committed offences punishable under Section 3(3) of TADA (P) Act, 1987 and Section 120B of IPC read with Sections 3(2)(i)(ii), 3(3)(4), 5 and 6 of TADA (P) Act, 1987 and read with Sections 302, 307, 326, 324, 427, 435, 436, 201 and 212 of Indian Penal Code and offences under Sections 3 and 7 read with Sections 25 (1A), (1B)(a) of the Arms Act, 1959, Sections 9B (1)(a)(b)(c) of the Explosives Act, 1884, Sections 3, 4(a)(b), 5 and 6 of the Explosive Substances Act, 1908 and Section 4 of the Prevention of Damage to Public Property Act, 1984 and within my cognizance.	Facts

Singh (A102), M.S. Sayyed (A90), Mohd.	None

Evidence The evidence against the appellant (A134) is in the form of (i) his own confession confessions made by other coconspirators (coaccused) testimony of prosecution witnesses and documentary evidence.	None

On return, those coaccused persons told the appellant that they had received weapons training at Pakistan and that they were met by Pakistani officers at the Airport who took them out without any immigration formalities.	None
The appellant was in Bombay on the day of the blasts but he denied the participation in the blasts.	None
He, however, fled to Bombay and stayed in Delhi, Uttar Pradesh and a neighbouring country and continued to work for Mohd.	None
Dossa in smuggling of gold.	None
In July, 1993, the appellant on the instructions of Mohd.	None
Dossa, removed AK56 rifles, hand grenades, small bombs and 2,000 cartridges lying with Ahmed Okliya of Surat, Gujarat.	None
These arms were the same which had landed at Dighi Jetty.	None
The appellant kept 1 AK56 rifle, 2 magazines and 88 cartridges with himself which were recovered by the police at the time of his arrest.	None
Upon perusal of the above confession of the appellant, the following facts emerge The appellant played an active role in the entire conspiracy viz., his meeting with Dawood Ibrahim in Dubai He participated in the landing at Dighi and subsequent transportation of arms and ammunitions He participated in the meeting and negotiations with Customs and Police officers in January, 1993 to seek permission and to fix the bribe amount for each landing.	None
He was a key aide of Mohd.	None
Dossa, who was one of the main co conspirators of the Bombay Bomb Blast case.	None
Though counsel for the appellant argued that his confession cannot be relied upon due to the fact that it was not voluntary, on going through the same and the procedure followed by the recording officer, we are satisfied that the appellant has made the above confession voluntarily, without any pressure or coercion and the same has been recorded after following all the safeguards enumerated under Section 15 of TADA and the rules framed thereunder.	None
The said facts have been duly established by the testimony of the recording officer PW481.	None

Criminal Appeal No. 401 of 2008 Mohd.	None
Kasam Lajpuria Mechanic Chacha (A136) Appellant(s) vs. The State of Maharashtra, through Superintendent of Police, CBISTF, Mumbai Respondent(s) WITH Criminal Appeal No. 1023 of 2012 The State of Maharashtra, through CBI .	None
