A perusal of the confessional statements of all the above accused, viz., A10, A12, A13, A16, A29, A32, A36, A39, A49, A52, A57, A 64 and A98 clearly establish the fact that it corroborate with the confessional statement of the appellant (A100).	Reasoning
After consideration of all the abovesaid confessional statements of the coaccused, the involvement of the appellant in the conspiracy is established inasmuch as The appellant participated in the landing at Shekhadi where arms and explosives were smuggled into India for the purpose of committing terrorist acts The appellant went to Pakistan via Dubai and participated in the weapons training The appellant participated in various conspiratorial meetings held in Dubai as well as in India including the meeting at the residence of A 96 where groups were made and final shape to the plan for blasts at various places in Bombay was discussed The appellant was a friend of Javed Chikna (AA)	None
The involvement of the appellant in the conspiracy was very deep	None
He participated in all the stages of conspiracy, namely, landing, training, planning etc.	None
and He was present at AlHussaini building on the night intervening 11/12.03.1993 when activity of filling of RDX in vehicles was going on.	None
Deposition of Prosecution Witnesses Apart from the aforesaid evidence, the involvement and the role of the appellant in the conspiracy as stated above is disclosed by the deposition of various prosecution witnesses which are as follows Deposition of Mohd.	Reasoning
Usman Jan Khan (PW2)	None
We have carefully gone through his evidence implicating the appellant (A100).	None
The relevant material in his evidence is as follows PW2 knew the appellant PW2 identified the appellant in Court The appellant participated in the landing at Shekhadi The appellant participated in weapons training at Pakistan After returning from the training camp to Dubai, at the instance of Tiger Memon, PW2 along with the appellant and others took oath of maintaining secrecy by swearing on the Quran The appellant was present in the conspiratorial meeting held at Shakils residence wherein Tiger Memon formed groups for surveying targets.	None
PW2, A64 and the appellant were in one group and were assigned the task of surveying Sena Bhavan and Sahar Airport PW2 went along with the appellant to survey Shiv Sena Bhavan and Sahar Airport on 08.03.1993, at which time, the appellant told him that he would not throw hand grenades on the Aircrafts at Sahar Airport since it was a dangerous assignment.	None
However, he expressed his willingness to do the work at Sena Bhavan The appellant participated in the conspiratorial meeting held at Babloos residence on 08.03.1993.	None
The above deposition of PW2, the Approver, corroborates with the confessional statements of the coaccused persons as well as the confession of the appellant.	None
The confession of the appellant read with the confessions of various coaccused persons along with the evidence of PW2 substantiate the charges framed against him.	None
Deposition of API A.S. Narote (PW243)	None
At the relevant time, PW243 was on Immigration duty and proved the departure of the appellant to Dubai from Bombay on 11.02.1993.	None
The relevant entries on the Embarkation Card (X400) concerning the departure have been marked as Exh.	None
Nos. 1053, 1053A, 1053A(1) and 1053A(2).	None
Deposition of PSI PE Ramgude (PW207) PW207 proved the arrival of the appellant to Bombay on 03.03.1993 from Dubai.	None
The relevant endorsements for the same are on the Disembarkation Card (X701).	None
Training in Pakistan With respect to the training at Pakistan, the confessional statements of coaccused persons against the appellant including his own confession are duly corroborated with the aforesaid depositions of the officers on Immigration duty who testified about the departure of the appellant to Dubai and his arrival at Bombay.	None
To undergo weapons training as a part of the conspiracy and to further the conspiracy to cause terrorist acts in India constitutes an offence.	None
The aforesaid evidence divulge that the appellant along with other coconspirators was given the said training to equip himself to commit terrorist acts in Bombay and, therefore, he was rightfully convicted for the same.	None
In view of the entire evidence enumerated above, we hold that the appellant was actively involved in the conspiracy to cause blasts in Bombay and in consequence of the said involvement, he had committed various offences.	Decision
Sentence The appellant was given full opportunity to defend himself on the question of quantum of sentence.	Facts
His statement was recorded on 10.10.2006 in which he prayed that the following factors, amongst others, may be considered while determining his sentence On the date of the incident, he was 26 years old and was selling bananas on the street He is suffering from a pancreatic ailment and dependent on drugs He has been in custody since his arrest except when he was released on interim bail on 3 occasions on the ground of medical treatment and During the bail period, he has not committed any offence or violated any condition imposed by the Court and during this period, he was earning his livelihood and bearing his medical expenses by selling bananas.	None
Ms. Farhana Shah, learned counsel appearing for the appellant while reiterating the same and after taking us through the confession made by the appellant and the confessional statements of coaccused, meticulously pointed out that even if we accept the prosecution case about the participation of the appellant in the training, unloading of weapons, visiting Dubai and Pakistan for training and participation in certain meetings, the appellant merely witnessed the filling of RDX and he was not one amongst the persons who filled all those explosive materials.	Arguments of Petitioner
With regard to the above, in the light of the evidence in the form of his own confession and confessional statement of coaccused persons, it cannot be claimed that he merely witnessed the incident when his presence is evidently proved by acceptable materials.	None
On the other hand, learned senior counsel appearing for the CBI pointed out that there is no need to show any leniency since after realizing explosions that had taken place in Bombay on 12.03.1993, the appellant (A100) had absconded and remained away from the clutches of law until he was arrested by the police.	Arguments of Respondent
It is also pointed out that so far he has served nearly 15 years as pointed out by the counsel for the appellant.	Arguments of Respondent
451) Before considering the claim of both the sides, it is useful to refer the conclusion of the Designated Judge while determining the quantum of sentence.	None
After stating all the details and narrating the entire events, the Designated Judge observed at page 41049 as under Thus in short though some leniency will be required to be shown to A100 due to himself having not continued till end of commission of final acts achieving the object of conspiracy, still he will be liable for the due punishment as warranted for the acts committed by him.	None
Taking note of the above observation of the Designated Judge and of the fact that that there is no dispute about his participation in the training, evidence disclosed that he associated in unloading of weapons and there is no need to show any leniency in awarding sentence.	None
Under these circumstances, we fully agree with the conclusion arrived at by the Designated Court, consequently, the appeals filed by the appellant herein (A100) are dismissed.	Decision
For convenience, we have reproduced the conclusion arrived at in respect of all the appeals dealt with under this part in Annexure A appended hereto.	Decision
